```sql
UPDATE bills
```

An empty string `''` is NOT NULL and is NOT IN the list = TRUE. So this condition passes.

Actually wait - let me re-check the flow in `SyncManager.performMasterPull()`:

```kotlin
suspend fun performMasterPull(): Result<Unit> {
    return syncMutex.withLock {
        try {
            ensureTerminalActivated()
            pullAndPersistMasterData(
                lastSyncTimestamp = sessionManager.getLastSyncTimestamp(),
                deviceId = sessionManager.getDeviceId()
            )
            // Re-label this terminal's own synced bills AFTER the pull
            masterSyncProcessor.reconcileLocalBillScope()
            return Result.success(Unit)
        } catch (e: Exception) {
            logError("Master pull failed", e)
            Result.failure(e)
        }
    }
}
```

This should work. `reconcileLocalBillScope` runs after the pull. But it's called within `performMasterPull()`, and `performMasterPull()` is called from `performFullSync()`:

```kotlin
suspend fun performFullSync(): Result<Unit> {
    stateMutex.withLock {
        if (isSyncing) {
            hasPendingSync = true
            return Result.success(Unit)
        }
        isSyncing = true
    }
    return try {
        ...
        pushAll()
        performMasterPull()
        ...
    }
}
```

So the full sync calls `pushAll()` first, then `performMasterPull()`. Inside `performMasterPull()`, my fix runs `reconcileLocalBillScope()` after the pull.

This should work. But the log shows the bill still has `recordOrigin=server_imported`. 

Hmm, let me reconsider. Maybe the `reconcileLocalBillScope` method has a bug. Let me look at it again:

```kotlin
suspend fun reconcileLocalBillScope() {
    val restaurantId = sessionManager.getRestaurantId()
    val terminalId = sessionManager.getTerminalId() ?: return
    if (restaurantId <= 0L) return
    val updated = billDao.reconcileLocalRecordScope(restaurantId, terminalId)
    if (updated > 0) {
        Log.i("MasterSyncProcessor", "Reconciled $updated local bill(s) to terminal_operational for terminal=$terminalId")
    }
```

```
196:     private suspend fun runSyncCycle(): Result<Unit> {
197:         // ── NonCancellable Guard ───────────────────────────────────────────────
198:         // Wrap the entire push+pull cycle in NonCancellable so that lifecycle
199:         // cancellations (screen rotation, app backgrounded, ViewModel cleared)
200:         // cannot abort a transaction mid-flight. An interrupted push leaves the
201:         // server SyncTransaction uncommitted → next attempt gets HTTP 409.
202:         return withContext(NonCancellable) {
203:             val deviceId = sessionManager.getDeviceId()
204:             val startedAt = System.currentTimeMillis()
205: 
206:             // ── Timestamp Race Fix (#2) ────────────────────────────────────────────
207:             // Capture the checkpoint BEFORE the sync cycle begins. This timestamp
208:             // is NOT written to persistent storage until the ENTIRE push+pull cycle
209:             // succeeds atomically in pullAndPersistMasterData(). If the push succeeds
210:             // but the pull fails, the checkpoint stays at the old value and the next
211:             // cycle re-pulls the missed window — no records are permanently lost.
```

## Assistant (Build · DeepSeek V4 Flash Free · 36.1s)

_Thinking:_

Good. The fix looks correct. Now `pullAndPersistMasterData()` calls `reconcileLocalBillScope()` right after `insertMasterData()`, which covers all three callers:

1. `performMasterPull()` (line 156) → calls `pullAndPersistMasterData()` → now gets reconciliation
2. `runSyncCycle()` (line 230) → calls `pullAndPersistMasterData()` → now gets reconciliation
3. `recoverFromSyncConflict()` (line 299) → calls `pullAndPersistMasterData(0L, deviceId)` → now gets reconciliation

Now, but will this fix the issue for a user who already has corrupted data? The reconcile query updates bills where:
- `restaurant_id = :restaurantId`
- `is_deleted = 0`
- `is_synced = 1`
- `created_terminal_id = :terminalId`
- `source_channel IS NULL OR source_channel NOT IN ('zomato', 'swiggy', 'own_website')`

For a fresh login (clear data), the pulled bills have `isSynced = true` from the server response. The reconcile query should run and fix them.

But wait - there's still a timing issue. The user clears data, logs in, the sync runs, fix applies. But when the user is actively using the app after login, the second sync (follow-up) runs and calls `pullAndPersistMasterData` again. If the second pull has 0 records (as we saw in the logs), then `insertMasterData` doesn't insert anything, and `reconcileLocalBillScope` runs again - but it's a no-op because bills are already reconciled.

However, there might be ANOTHER subtle issue. What if `reconcileLocalBillScope()` is running before `insertMasterData` has fully committed? Since Room DAO methods with `@Transaction` should be synchronous from the caller's perspective, that shouldn't be a problem. But let me check.

Actually, both `insertMasterData` and `reconcileLocalBillScope` are suspend functions that interact with Room. Room's `@Transaction` methods are fully synchronous with respect to the calling coroutine. So the reconcile should see all the inserted data.

OK, I think the fix is correct now. Let me also check if there's still the `insertSyncedBills` fix I made earlier that preserves localBill.recordOrigin/recordScope - that fix is also important because it handles the case where a local bill exists and the remote overwrites it. But the larger issue is that on fresh login, there's NO local bill - the bill comes entirely from the server. In that case, `insertSyncedBills` inserts the bill as-is from the server (with `server_imported`/`restaurant_history`), and then `reconcileLocalBillScope` should fix it.

Let me also verify the `insertSyncedBills` fix one more time and the `reconcileLocalRecordScope` query to make sure both layers work together.

Let me build the APK and tell the user to test.

The fix now ensures `reconcileLocalBillScope()` runs after EVERY pull path:

- `runSyncCycle()` (main sync loop) — **was missing reconcile** ← root cause
- `recoverFromSyncConflict()` (409 conflict recovery) — **was missing reconcile** ← secondary path
- `performMasterPull()` — was already reconciled

All three call `pullAndPersistMasterData()`, which now calls `reconcileLocalBillScope()` right after `insertMasterData()`.

2. Runs the lambda
3. If lambda succeeds, marks the transaction as successful
4. Ends the transaction (commits)
5. Returns the lambda's result

---

## Objective
- Fix editing payment mode and status on existing same-day bills in the Android app (currently silently fails)

## Important Details
- Root cause: `getOperationalBillById` (`BillDao.kt:133`) requires `recordOrigin=local_created` AND `recordScope=terminal_operational`, but the sync pull (`insertSyncedBills`) sets them to `server_imported`/`restaurant_history`. This makes `updatePaymentMode` / `updateOrderStatus` return null and silently exit.
- Logcat confirms: bill `id=206` has `recordOrigin=server_imported recordScope=restaurant_history` even though `createdTerminalId=12` and `currentOwnerTerminalId=12` match the terminal. `getOperationalBillById` returns null.
- Fix attempts (1 & 2) tried to preserve labels via `insertSyncedBills` + `reconcileLocalBillScope`, but on re-login the local DB already had the corrupted label from the prior session, so preserving it didn't help.

## Work State
### Completed
- **Fix #3 (the real fix)**: Changed `getOperationalBillById` to use `currentOwnerTerminalId` + marketplace exclusion (`sourceChannel NOT IN ('zomato','swiggy','own_website')`) instead of checking `recordOrigin`/`recordScope`. This is the correct gate — terminal ownership is proven by `currentOwnerTerminalId`, not fragile label fields.
- Reverted `insertSyncedBills` — no longer preserves stale local `recordOrigin`/`recordScope` (fix #1 is rolled back).
- Moved `reconcileLocalBillScope()` into `pullAndPersistMasterData()` (fix #2 stays) so it runs after every pull path for data-model consistency.
- Added unconditional logging to `reconcileLocalBillScope()` for visibility.

### Active
- User testing with new APK built at `2026-07-20 13:17`.

### Blocked
- (none)

## Next Move
1. Install new APK and test editing payment mode on bill 206 (or any same-day bill)
2. Confirm via logcat that `getOperationalBillById` now returns a non-null result for bills with `recordOrigin=server_imported`

## Relevant Files
- `Android/.../data/local/dao/BillDao.kt`: `getOperationalBillById` (line 133) — **the fix**, `insertSyncedBills` (line 662) — reverted, `reconcileLocalRecordScope` (line 147)
- `Android/.../data/repository/BillRepository.kt`: `updatePaymentMode` (line 221), `currentTerminalScope` (line 32)
- `Android/.../domain/manager/SyncManager.kt`: `pullAndPersistMasterData` (line 278) — now calls reconcile
- `Android/.../domain/manager/MasterSyncProcessor.kt`: `reconcileLocalBillScope` (line 132) — unconditional logging added

_Thinking:_

The user is asking how to fix this issue. They want me to explain the solution. Let me give a concise answer.

The fix changes `getOperationalBillById` in `BillDao.kt:133` to stop checking `recordOrigin`/`recordScope`. Those fields get overwritten by sync pull to `server_imported`/`restaurant_history`, making bills appear non-editable. Instead, the query now uses `currentOwnerTerminalId` (which already proves terminal ownership) plus a marketplace exclusion (`sourceChannel NOT IN ('zomato','swiggy','own_website')`) to block edits on delivery-app orders.

Install the new APK and test editing the payment mode on bill 206.

## User

This image is a **large Entity–Relationship Diagram (ERD)** for a restaurant/POS platform database, likely the **KhanaBook backend PostgreSQL database**. All the tables appear under the `public` schema.

## Overall structure

The database is designed as a **multi-tenant restaurant management system**. Most operational tables appear to contain a `restaurant_id`, which separates each restaurant’s data.

The diagram contains several major business areas:

### 1. Restaurant and organisation management

The upper-left section contains the main business entities, including tables related to:

* Restaurants
* Organisations or business owners
* Restaurant registration/onboarding
* Restaurant partners
* Business and contact details
* Approval and verification status
* Payment onboarding or merchant configuration

These tables store information such as restaurant names, addresses, phone numbers, registration status, ownership information and timestamps.

The restaurant or organisation record appears to be one of the central parent entities in the database.

### 2. User authentication and security

The upper-right section contains authentication and security-related tables, including identifiable tables such as:

* `users`
* `user_devices`
* `security_audit_log`
* Password or reset-token-related records
* User-to-restaurant access configuration
* Login or authentication history

The `users` table appears to store fields such as:

* User ID
* Restaurant ID
* Name
* Email
* Phone number
* Password hash
* Role
* Active/locked status
* Login information
* Created and updated timestamps

The `security_audit_log` table records security-sensitive activities, likely including login events, terminal overrides, access attempts and administrative activity.

### 3. Terminal and device management

Several tables represent POS terminals and registered devices.

They appear to store:

* Terminal ID
* Restaurant ID
* Device identifier
* Terminal name or terminal series
* Activation status
* Public or recovery token
* Last activity
* Device ownership
* Created and updated timestamps

This section supports the multi-terminal design where each restaurant can operate several billing devices while keeping terminal-level identity and invoice sequences.

### 4. Billing and order management

The largest connected section on the left and lower-left appears to be the core POS transaction model.

It contains tables related to:

* Bills or invoices
* Bill items
* Bill payments
* Orders
* Order items
* Active and completed orders
* Discounts
* Taxes
* Refunds
* Payment modes
* Customer information
* Dine-in, takeaway and online orders

A typical relationship represented here is:

```text
Restaurant
   └── Bill / Order
          ├── Bill Items
          ├── Payments
          ├── Taxes
          ├── Discounts
          └── Refund or settlement information
```

The main transaction tables are very large because they contain information such as:

* Restaurant and terminal IDs
* Invoice number
* Local and server IDs
* Customer details
* Order source
* Order type
* Subtotal
* Tax
* Discount
* Grand total
* Payment status
* Sync status
* KOT status
* Created, modified and finalized timestamps

### 5. Menu and product management

The schema also appears to include tables for:

* Menu categories
* Menu items
* Item variants
* Prices
* Add-ons
* Tax configuration
* Availability
* Restaurant-specific product settings

The probable hierarchy is:

```text
Restaurant
   └── Category
          └── Menu Item
                 ├── Variant
                 ├── Add-on
                 └── Price/tax configuration
```

### 6. KOT and kitchen operations

Tables related to **Kitchen Order Tickets** appear to connect orders, bill items and terminal information.

These likely support:

* Initial KOT creation
* Updated KOTs
* Item quantities
* Kitchen status
* Printer routing
* Sent-to-kitchen status
* Cancellation or modification tracking

This is important for maintaining an audit trail when items are added to an existing order after the first KOT is printed.

### 7. Inventory management

The operational portion also appears to include inventory-related entities for:

* Stock items
* Inventory quantity
* Stock movement
* Low-stock thresholds
* Units of measurement
* Item-to-inventory mapping
* Restaurant-level inventory records

These records would allow menu sales to reduce inventory and generate low-stock notifications.

### 8. Payment and merchant configuration

The upper portion includes payment-related configuration tables that likely store:

* Merchant or sub-merchant IDs
* Payment provider configuration
* Payment mode
* Onboarding status
* KYC or verification status
* Settlement settings
* Provider-specific references

This is probably connected to the Easebuzz sub-merchant onboarding and payment workflow.

### 9. Audit, status and synchronization

Many tables contain fields that appear to follow an offline-sync pattern:

* `local_id`
* Server ID or UUID
* `restaurant_id`
* `terminal_id`
* `created_at`
* `updated_at`
* Sync status
* Deleted or active flag
* Version or revision information

This structure supports Android devices creating records offline and later synchronizing them with the backend.

## Relationship patterns

The diagram uses:

* **Yellow key icon:** primary key
* **Link/relationship lines:** foreign-key relationships
* **Green/blue field icons:** regular columns and typed fields
* **Long vertical relationship lines:** references between business modules

Most relationships appear to follow a parent-child structure:

```text
Organisation
   └── Restaurant
          ├── Users
          ├── Terminals
          ├── Menu
          ├── Customers
          ├── Orders
          ├── Bills
          ├── Payments
          └── Inventory
```

## Important architectural observation

The schema is comprehensive, but visually it is highly spread out. Some related tables are far apart, creating long relationship lines and a large unused central area. For technical review, it would be easier to separate this into smaller ERDs:

1. Authentication and security
2. Restaurant and onboarding
3. Menu and inventory
4. Billing and payments
5. Orders and KOT
6. Terminal and synchronization

The supplied image resolution is sufficient to understand the architecture, but several individual table and column names are too small to read reliably. Therefore, this is a high-level functional description rather than an exact table-by-table data dictionary.

```
<path>C:\Users\nandh\Desktop\Khanabook\KhanaBook\server\src\main\resources\db\migration\V11__fix_date_column_and_salt_constraint.sql</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>
1: -- FIX #12: restaurantprofiles.last_reset_date VARCHAR → DATE migration
2: -- The VARCHAR column is fragile: "2026-4-1" ≠ "2026-04-01" so date comparisons
3: -- for daily counter resets can silently fail. We backfill the new DATE column
4: -- from the existing VARCHAR and then add a NOT NULL constraint.
5: --
6: -- The new column last_reset_date_proper (DATE) was added in V1 but left nullable.
7: -- This migration backfills it from last_reset_date (VARCHAR) where missing,
8: -- then enforces NOT NULL going forward.
9: 
10: -- Step 1: Backfill any NULLs in the proper DATE column from the VARCHAR column.
11: -- We cast via TO_DATE with a safe fallback to today's date if the VARCHAR is malformed.
12: UPDATE restaurantprofiles
13: SET last_reset_date_proper = (
14:     CASE
15:         WHEN last_reset_date IS NOT NULL AND last_reset_date ~ '^\d{4}-\d{1,2}-\d{1,2}$'
16:         THEN TO_DATE(last_reset_date, 'YYYY-MM-DD')
17:         ELSE CURRENT_DATE
18:     END
19: )
20: WHERE last_reset_date_proper IS NULL;
21: 
22: -- Step 2: Enforce NOT NULL now that all rows are backfilled.
23: ALTER TABLE restaurantprofiles
24:     ALTER COLUMN last_reset_date_proper SET NOT NULL,
25:     ALTER COLUMN last_reset_date_proper SET DEFAULT CURRENT_DATE;
26: 
27: -- FIX #5: Validate encrypted_salt is non-trivially encrypted.
28: -- We cannot enforce AES-GCM in SQL, but we can enforce minimum length
29: -- (a real AES-GCM/Base64 ciphertext is always >32 chars) and reject
30: -- values that look like plain phone numbers (all digits, <20 chars).
31: ALTER TABLE restaurant_payment_config
32:     ADD CONSTRAINT chk_encrypted_salt_looks_encrypted
33:     CHECK (
34:         encrypted_salt IS NULL
35:         OR (
36:             LENGTH(encrypted_salt) >= 32
37:             AND encrypted_salt !~ '^\d+$'
38:         )
39:     );
40: 
41: -- Add a comment documenting the expected format.
42: COMMENT ON COLUMN restaurant_payment_config.encrypted_salt
43:     IS 'AES-GCM encrypted, Base64-encoded salt. Must be ≥32 chars. Plain text values are rejected by chk_encrypted_salt_looks_encrypted.';

(End of file - total 43 lines)
</content>
```

```
12: UPDATE bills b
13: SET payment_mode = 'easebuzz'
14: WHERE payment_mode = 'upi'
15:   AND EXISTS (
16:       SELECT 1 FROM bill_payments bp
17:       WHERE bp.bill_id = b.id
18:         AND bp.verified_by = 'easebuzz'
19:   );
20: 
21: -- 3. bills: part_cash_upi → part_cash_easebuzz where the UPI leg was gateway-paid
22: UPDATE bills b
23: SET payment_mode = 'part_cash_easebuzz'
24: WHERE payment_mode = 'part_cash_upi'
25:   AND EXISTS (
26:       SELECT 1 FROM bill_payments bp
27:       WHERE bp.bill_id = b.id
28:         AND bp.verified_by = 'easebuzz'
29:   );
30: 
31: -- 4. bills: part_upi_pos → part_easebuzz_pos where the UPI leg was gateway-paid
32: UPDATE bills b
33: SET payment_mode = 'part_easebuzz_pos'
34: WHERE payment_mode = 'part_upi_pos'
35:   AND EXISTS (
36:       SELECT 1 FROM bill_payments bp
37:       WHERE bp.bill_id = b.id
38:         AND bp.verified_by = 'easebuzz'
39:   );
```

**Output:**
```
<path>C:\Users\nandh\Desktop\Khanabook\KhanaBook\server\src\main\resources\db\migration\V23__dedup_bill_payments_gateway_txn.sql</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>
1: -- Deduplicate gateway-owned bill payments.
2: -- payments.gateway_txn_id is already UNIQUE (V7). bill_payments carries the same
3: -- gateway_txn_id for gateway-verified payments but had no uniqueness guard, so a
4: -- WorkManager retry after a dropped push response could insert a duplicate row.
5: -- A partial unique index enforces one active row per non-blank gateway_txn_id while
6: -- still allowing many manual (NULL) payments. Paired with an app-layer idempotency skip
7: -- in GenericSyncService so a retried push is ignored rather than failing the batch.
8: 
9: -- Safety net: collapse any pre-existing duplicates before the index is created,
10: -- keeping the earliest row (lowest id) and soft-deleting the rest. Without this,
11: -- the CREATE UNIQUE INDEX statement would fail on existing duplicates.
12: UPDATE bill_payments bp
13: SET is_deleted = TRUE
14: WHERE bp.id IN (
15:     SELECT other.id
16:     FROM bill_payments other
17:     WHERE other.gateway_txn_id IS NOT NULL
18:       AND other.gateway_txn_id <> ''
19:       AND other.is_deleted = FALSE
20:       AND other.gateway_txn_id = bp.gateway_txn_id
21:       AND other.restaurant_id = bp.restaurant_id
22:       AND other.id > bp.id
23: );
24: 
25: -- Enforce one *active* row per non-blank gateway_txn_id. Scoping the predicate to
26: -- is_deleted = FALSE keeps it consistent with the soft-delete dedup above and
27: -- lets a legitimately re-created payment reuse a txn id whose prior row was
28: -- soft-deleted.
29: CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS uq_bill_payments_gateway_txn
30:     ON bill_payments (gateway_txn_id)
31:     WHERE gateway_txn_id IS NOT NULL AND gateway_txn_id <> '' AND is_deleted = FALSE;

(End of file - total 31 lines)
</content>
```

## Key findings

### Missing FK constraints (notable)
- `bill_items.bill_id` → `bills.id` has a tenant-scoped FK (V3), good
- `bill_payments.bill_id` → `bills.id` has a tenant-scoped FK (V3), good
- `payments.bill_id` → `bills.id` has **NO FK** at all (V7) — orphaned payments possible
- `marketplace_orders.restaurant_id` → `restaurantprofiles.id` uses single-column FK (V21) — should be tenant-scoped but `restaurantprofiles` has no `(restaurant_id, id)` unique index to support it
- `device_registration_request.restaurant_id` / `requested_by_user_id` have **NO FKs** (V41)

### Tenant isolation
Most tables use `restaurant_id` everywhere, and V3 hardened FKs to composite `(restaurant_id, id)`. Good. But V7's `payments` table and V41's `device_registration_request` are missing this pattern.

### Offline-sync pattern
All V1 tables follow `(restaurant_id, device_id, local_id)` as the offline identity key. Later tables (V7, V8, V26, V41) use `BIGSERIAL` server-only IDs — these are **not synced to Android** and only live server-side.

### Terminal ownership (bills)
V28 added `created_terminal_id`, `current_owner_terminal_id`, `created_device_id` and backfilled from legacy `terminal_id`/`terminal_series`. V40 added `terminal_id` to all sync tables and backfilled via `restaurant_terminal` join.

### Invoice numbering (bills)
V26 added `terminal_series`, `financial_year`, `invoice_series`, `invoice_sequence`, `invoice_number` and made `lifetime_order_id` nullable. Dropped V22's legacy uniqueness indexes in favour of series-aware ones.

### Potential issues
1. **`payments` table has no restaurant-scoped FK to bills** — `payments.bill_id` could reference a bill from another restaurant
2. **`device_registration_request` has no FK** to `restaurant_terminal` or `users`
3. **V12 collapsed MANAGER/CASHIER/KITCHEN roles to OWNER** — role distinction is gone server-side (Android may still use these)
4. **`source_channel` added in V25** — backfill only sets it for known marketplace payment modes. In-store POS bills remain blank
5. **V27 and V30-V39 are missing** — 11 version numbers skipped, possibly removed/rebased

## User

This is a strong migration review, but a few conclusions need correction or deeper verification before changing the schema.

## Important corrections

### 1. The table count does not match the inventory

The report says **31 tables**, but the inventory shown contains only **23 tables**.

Ask the tool to list the remaining eight tables or correct the count. This matters because omitted tables may contain additional foreign keys, indexes, audit data or legacy structures.

### 2. `marketplace_orders.restaurant_id` is probably not a tenant-scoping problem

This relationship:

```text
marketplace_orders.restaurant_id → restaurantprofiles.id
```

is normally correct because `restaurantprofiles` is the tenant/root table. A composite foreign key is not needed when referencing the restaurant itself.

Composite tenant-scoped foreign keys are mainly important for child-to-child relationships, such as:

```text
bill_items(restaurant_id, bill_id)
    → bills(restaurant_id, id)
```

They prevent a child record belonging to Restaurant A from referencing a bill belonging to Restaurant B.

So this should not be reported as a defect unless `marketplace_orders` references another tenant-owned child entity using only its ID.

### 3. Missing Flyway version numbers are not automatically a problem

Missing versions such as:

```text
V27
V30–V39
```

are valid in Flyway. Migration numbering does not need to be continuous.

It becomes a problem only when:

* those migrations existed in an already-deployed environment and were later deleted;
* production has entries for them in `flyway_schema_history`;
* the codebase was rebased and migration history now differs between environments;
* the missing versions contain required schema changes.

The correct verification is:

```sql
SELECT installed_rank,
       version,
       description,
       script,
       checksum,
       success
FROM flyway_schema_history
ORDER BY installed_rank;
```

Compare this output across development, staging and production.

## Confirmed high-priority risks

### 1. `payments.bill_id` without tenant-scoped FK

This is the most serious finding.

Without a constraint, the database may allow:

* orphan payments;
* payment records referencing deleted bills;
* Restaurant A payment referencing Restaurant B bill;
* incorrect settlement, refund or reconciliation data.

The preferred relationship is:

```sql
FOREIGN KEY (restaurant_id, bill_id)
REFERENCES bills (restaurant_id, id)
```

Before adding it, check existing invalid records:

```sql
SELECT p.id,
       p.restaurant_id,
       p.bill_id,
       b.restaurant_id AS bill_restaurant_id
FROM payments p
LEFT JOIN bills b ON b.id = p.bill_id
WHERE p.bill_id IS NOT NULL
  AND (
      b.id IS NULL
      OR b.restaurant_id <> p.restaurant_id
  );
```

Do not add the constraint until these rows are reviewed and corrected.

### 2. `device_registration_request` integrity

At minimum, verify these relationships:

```text
restaurant_id → restaurantprofiles.id
requested_by_user_id → users.id
```

The user relationship should ideally be tenant-scoped:

```text
(restaurant_id, requested_by_user_id)
    → users(restaurant_id, id)
```

This ensures a user from another restaurant cannot create or approve a device request.

A terminal foreign key is required only if the table actually stores a terminal reference such as:

```text
terminal_id
approved_terminal_id
recovered_terminal_id
```

Do not claim it needs a `restaurant_terminal` FK unless such a column exists.

### 3. Role collapse in V12

Changing:

```text
MANAGER
CASHIER
KITCHEN
```

to:

```text
OWNER
```

is not necessarily a schema bug, but it is a major authorization concern.

Verify:

* whether the backend enum still contains the old roles;
* whether Android sends or expects those roles;
* whether endpoint authorization uses `OWNER` only;
* whether permissions are now terminal-based instead;
* whether previously restricted users gained owner-level access;
* whether the migration permanently destroyed role information.

The critical question is not merely whether the role names disappeared. It is whether **privilege boundaries disappeared**.

### 4. Blank `source_channel`

Leaving in-store bills blank creates ambiguous reporting and conditional logic.

A safer model is usually:

```text
POS
ZOMATO
SWIGGY
CUSTOMER_APP
MANUAL
OTHER
```

For existing ordinary bills, the migration could potentially backfill:

```sql
source_channel = 'POS'
```

But first verify whether `NULL` currently has a deliberate meaning such as “legacy/unknown.” Do not blindly convert historical data.

## Additional checks missing from the review

The review should also verify the following.

### Delete behaviour

For every foreign key, document whether it uses:

```text
ON DELETE RESTRICT
ON DELETE CASCADE
ON DELETE SET NULL
NO ACTION
```

Dangerous cascade behaviour around bills, payments, refunds and audit records could cause financial records to disappear.

### Index support

Every frequently queried foreign key should be checked for a supporting index, especially:

```text
payments(restaurant_id, bill_id)
bill_items(restaurant_id, bill_id)
bill_payments(restaurant_id, bill_id)
bills(restaurant_id, current_owner_terminal_id)
bills(restaurant_id, invoice_number)
device_registration_request(restaurant_id, status)
security_audit_log(restaurant_id, created_at)
marketplace_orders(restaurant_id, external_order_id)
```

A foreign key does not automatically create an index in PostgreSQL.

### Tenant-safe unique constraints

Verify that tenant-owned business identifiers are not globally unique unless intentionally global.

Examples:

```text
category name
menu item code
invoice number
external order ID
terminal series
device ID
payment transaction ID
```

Many should be unique within a restaurant or provider scope rather than across the entire database.

### Soft-delete consistency

If tables use fields such as:

```text
deleted
is_active
deleted_at
status
```

check whether unique indexes account for deleted rows through partial indexes.

For example:

```sql
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX ...
ON categories (restaurant_id, lower(name))
WHERE deleted = false;
```

### Terminal backfill reliability

V40 reportedly backfilled `terminal_id` through a join to `restaurant_terminal`. Verify:

* rows that did not match any terminal;
* restaurants with duplicate device identifiers;
* bills where legacy `terminal_id` conflicts with `created_terminal_id`;
* nullable terminal IDs after backfill;
* whether the migration silently selected one terminal from multiple matches.

Useful checks include:

```sql
SELECT COUNT(*)
FROM bills
WHERE terminal_id IS NULL;
```

and similar checks for every sync table modified by V40.

## Recommended priority

**P0 — Verify immediately**

1. Cross-tenant or orphaned rows in `payments`.
2. Authorization impact of V12 role collapse.
3. Cross-tenant device registration requests.
4. Deleted or divergent Flyway migrations across environments.

**P1 — Fix before production expansion**

1. Add validated foreign keys.
2. Backfill and standardize `source_channel`.
3. Add missing indexes.
4. Validate terminal backfill completeness.
5. Review cascade rules.

**P2 — Maintainability**

1. Correct the table inventory.
2. Produce a complete schema dictionary.
3. Mark server-only versus Android-synced tables.
4. Document legacy columns and planned removal.

A better final conclusion would be:

> The schema generally applies restaurant-scoped isolation well, especially after V3 and the terminal migrations. The clearest integrity gap is the unscoped `payments.bill_id` relationship. Device registration authorization and the V12 role migration require application-level review. Marketplace-to-restaurant single-column foreign keys and skipped Flyway version numbers are not defects by themselves.

---

```
## Full JPA Entity Relationship & Cascade Analysis

### Entity Inventory

All 15 JPA entities found under `com.khanabook.saas.entity`:

| # | Class | `@Entity` (default name) | `@Table` name |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | `User` | `User` | `users` |
| 2 | `RestaurantProfile` | `RestaurantProfile` | `restaurantprofiles` |
| 3 | `Category` | `Category` | `categories` |
| 4 | `MenuItem` | `MenuItem` | `menuitems` |
| 5 | `ItemVariant` | `ItemVariant` | `itemvariants` |
| 6 | `Bill` | `Bill` | `bills` |
| 7 | `BillItem` | `BillItem` | `bill_items` |
| 8 | `BillPayment` | `BillPayment` | `bill_payments` |
| 9 | `StockLog` | `StockLog` | `stock_logs` |
| 10 | `DeviceRegistrationRequest` | `DeviceRegistrationRequest` | `device_registration_request` |
| 11 | `RestaurantTerminal` | `RestaurantTerminal` | `restaurant_terminal` |
| 12 | `SecurityAuditEvent` | `SecurityAuditEvent` | `security_audit_log` |
| 13 | `TokenBlocklist` | `TokenBlocklist` | `token_blocklist` |
| 14 | `OtpRequest` | `OtpRequest` | `otp_requests` |
| 15 | `MenuExtractionJob` | `MenuExtractionJob` | `menu_extraction_jobs` |

Base superclass: `BaseSyncEntity` (a `@MappedSuperclass`, not an entity itself). All sync entities inherit `id`, `localId`, `deviceId`, `terminalId`, `restaurantId`, `updatedAt`, `isDeleted`, `serverUpdatedAt`, `createdAt`, and `version`.

**Tables without JPA entities** (managed via native queries/repositories only): `payments`, `restaurant_payment_config`, `payment_webhook_logs`, `easebuzz_webhook_events`, `marketplace_orders`, `marketplace_order_items`, `customer_orders`, `customer_order_items`.

---

### All `@ManyToOne` / `@JoinColumn` Annotations

#### 1. `MenuItem.category` → `Category`

- **Field**: `MenuItem.serverCategoryId` (raw FK column) + `MenuItem.category` (`@ManyToOne` LAZY)
- **Join column**: `server_category_id` → `categories.id`
- **`@JoinColumn`**: `insertable = false, updatable = false` (read-only — the real FK is `category_id`; this is a soft link)
- **`cascade`**: NONE
- **`orphanRemoval`**: NONE
- **`@OnDelete`**: NONE
- **Flyway FK** (`fk_menuitems_category_tenant`, V1→V3):
  - `ON DELETE RESTRICT` (tenant-scoped composite FK on `(restaurant_id, server_category_id)`)
  - **MISMATCH**: JPA has no cascade/delete behavior. The DB has `RESTRICT`. The JPA `MenuItem` entity will never cascade a delete to `Category` (no `cascade` attribute), which is correct — you should NOT delete a category if menu items reference it. But there is no `@OnDelete(action = OnDeleteAction.NO_ACTION)` or `@OnDelete(action = OnDeleteAction.RESTRICT)` on the JPA side to document this. Since `insertable=false, updatable=false`, Hibernate does not manage this FK at all for writes; it is purely a read-relationship for JSON serialization on pull.

#### 2. `ItemVariant.menuItem` → `MenuItem`

- **Field**: `ItemVariant.serverMenuItemId` (raw FK) + `ItemVariant.menuItem` (`@ManyToOne` LAZY)
- **Join column**: `server_menu_item_id` → `menuitems.id`
- **`@JoinColumn`**: `insertable = false, updatable = false`
- **`cascade`**: NONE
- **`orphanRemoval`**: NONE
- **`@OnDelete`**: NONE
- **Flyway FK** (`fk_itemvariants_menuitem_tenant`, V1→V3):
  - Original V1: `ON DELETE SET NULL DEFERRABLE INITIALLY DEFERRED`
  - V3 (hardened): `ON DELETE RESTRICT` (tenant-scoped composite FK)
  - **MISMATCH**: JPA has no cascade/delete behavior. The DB has `RESTRICT`. If a `MenuItem` is deleted from the DB directly (not through Hibernate), the FK prevents it if variants reference it. Again, since `insertable=false, updatable=false`, Hibernate does not manage this for writes — it is read-only.

#### 3. `BillItem.bill` → `Bill`

- **Field**: `BillItem.serverBillId` (raw FK) + `BillItem.bill` (`@ManyToOne` LAZY)
- **Join column**: `server_bill_id` → `bills.id`
- **`@JoinColumn`**: `insertable = false, updatable = false`
- **`cascade`**: NONE
- **`orphanRemoval`**: NONE
- **`@OnDelete`**: NONE
- **Flyway FK** for `bill_id` (the real column):
  - V1: `fk_bill_items_bill` on `(bill_id)` → `ON DELETE CASCADE`
  - V3: Replaced with `fk_bill_items_bill_tenant` on `(restaurant_id, bill_id)` → `ON DELETE CASCADE`
  - **CRITICAL**: The JPA entity has **NO cascade** on the `@ManyToOne` and **NO `@OnDelete`**. But the DB FK cascades deletes automatically. If a `Bill` row is deleted from the database, all its `bill_items` rows are cascade-deleted by the DB trigger — even though Hibernate knows nothing about it. The `@ManyToOne` targets `server_bill_id` (which is `insertable=false, updatable=false`, a secondary reference that may be NULL). The *real* FK used for cascade is `bill_id` (not mapped as a JPA relationship at all, only as a plain `@Column`).
  - **BIG GAP**: The `bill_id` column has `ON DELETE CASCADE` in the DB but the JPA entity has no `@OnDelete(action = ON_DELETE.CASCADE)` annotation. Hibernate's own cascade settings are entirely absent. If Hibernate issues a `DELETE FROM bills WHERE id=?`, the DB cascade handles child cleanup — but if the entity has collections with `cascade` or `orphanRemoval`, there could be double-delete attempts (harmless in this case since no collections exist).

#### 4. `BillItem.menuItem` → `MenuItem`

- **Field**: `BillItem.serverMenuItemId` (raw FK) + `BillItem.menuItem` (`@ManyToOne` LAZY)
- **Join column**: `server_menu_item_id` → `menuitems.id`
- **`@JoinColumn`**: `insertable = false, updatable = false`
- **`cascade`**: NONE
- **`orphanRemoval`**: NONE
- **`@OnDelete`**: NONE
- **Flyway FK**:
  - V1: `fk_bill_items_menuitem` on `(server_menu_item_id)` → `ON DELETE SET NULL DEFERRABLE INITIALLY DEFERRED`
  - V3: Replaced with `fk_bill_items_menuitem_tenant` on `(restaurant_id, server_menu_item_id)` → `ON DELETE RESTRICT`
  - **MISMATCH**: DB now has `RESTRICT`, JPA has nothing. Since `insertable=false, updatable=false`, Hibernate never writes this. If a `MenuItem` is deleted, the DB now prevents it (RESTRICT) rather than setting NULL. This was a deliberate hardening in V3.

#### 5. `BillPayment.bill` → `Bill`

- **Field**: `BillPayment.serverBillId` (raw FK) + `BillPayment.bill` (`@ManyToOne` LAZY)
- **Join column**: `server_bill_id` → `bills.id`
- **`@JoinColumn`**: `insertable = false, updatable = false`
- **`cascade`**: NONE
- **`orphanRemoval`**: NONE
- **`@OnDelete`**: NONE
- **Flyway FK** for `bill_id` (the real column):
  - V1: `fk_bill_payments_bill` on `(bill_id)` → `ON DELETE CASCADE`
  - V3: Replaced with `fk_bill_payments_bill_tenant` on `(restaurant_id, bill_id)` → `ON DELETE CASCADE`
  - **CRITICAL**: Same pattern as `bill_items`. The `@ManyToOne` targets `server_bill_id` (secondary, nullable, `insertable=false`). The real FK column `bill_id` (which is `@Column(nullable=false)`) has `ON DELETE CASCADE` in the DB but is **not** mapped as a JPA relationship. No `@OnDelete` annotation.

#### 6. `StockLog.menuItem` → `MenuItem`

- **Field**: `StockLog.serverMenuItemId` (raw FK) + `StockLog.menuItem` (`@ManyToOne` LAZY)
- **Join column**: `server_menu_item_id` → `menuitems.id`
- **`@JoinColumn`**: `insertable = false, updatable = false`
- **`cascade`**: NONE
- **`orphanRemoval`**: NONE
- **`@OnDelete`**: NONE
- **Flyway FK**:
  - V1: `fk_stock_logs_menuitem` on `(server_menu_item_id)` → `ON DELETE SET NULL DEFERRABLE INITIALLY DEFERRED`
  - V3: Replaced with `fk_stock_logs_menuitem_tenant` on `(restaurant_id, server_menu_item_id)` → `ON DELETE RESTRICT`
  - **MISMATCH**: DB has RESTRICT, JPA has nothing. Read-only relationship.

#### 7. `StockLog.itemVariant` → `ItemVariant`

- **Field**: `StockLog.serverVariantId` (raw FK) + `StockLog.itemVariant` (`@ManyToOne` LAZY)
- **Join column**: `server_variant_id` → `itemvariants.id`
- **`@JoinColumn`**: `insertable = false, updatable = false`
- **`cascade`**: NONE
- **`orphanRemoval`**: NONE
- **`@OnDelete`**: NONE
- **Flyway FK**:
  - V1: `fk_stock_logs_variant` on `(server_variant_id)` → `ON DELETE SET NULL DEFERRABLE INITIALLY DEFERRED`
  - V3: Replaced with `fk_stock_logs_variant_tenant` on `(restaurant_id, server_variant_id)` → `ON DELETE RESTRICT`
  - Same pattern: RESTRICT in DB, nothing in JPA.

---

### `@OneToMany` Annotations

**None found.** No entity declares a `@OneToMany` or `@ManyToMany` collection. All child relationships (bill_items → bill, bill_payments → bill, etc.) are unidirectional parent→child only (from the child side). There are no `cascade` or `orphanRemoval` directives anywhere in the codebase.

---

### `@OnDelete` Annotations

**None found.** No entity uses `@OnDelete(action = ...)`. This means Hibernate DDL generation (if `ddl-auto` were enabled) would produce no `ON DELETE` clauses. The actual FK rules come solely from Flyway migrations.

---

### Focus Areas: Detailed Analysis

#### A. `payments` → `bills` (V7 table, NO JPA entity)

- **Table**: `payments` (created in V7, no `@Entity` anywhere)
- **FK**: `bill_id` → `bills(id)` — but **no FK constraint is defined** in V7! The column `bill_id BIGINT NOT NULL` has no `REFERENCES` clause.
- **Impact**: Orphan `payments` rows can exist if a bill is deleted. Since there's no JPA entity, Hibernate never deletes through this path. If a bill is cascade-deleted (from bill_items/bill_payments), the `payments` table is untouched. This is a **data integrity gap** — payments could reference non-existent bills.
- **No cascade, no JPA entity, no FK constraint at all.** This is the most notable gap in financial record safety.

#### B. `bill_items` → `bills`, `bill_items` → `menuitems`, `bill_items` → `itemvariants`

| Relationship | JPA `@ManyToOne` | `cascade` | `orphanRemoval` | `@OnDelete` | DB FK | DB `ON DELETE` |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| `bill_items` → `bills` (via `bill_id`) | NO (bare `@Column`) | — | — | — | `fk_bill_items_bill_tenant` (V3) | **CASCADE** |
| `bill_items` → `bills` (via `server_bill_id`) | YES (LAZY, read-only) | NONE | NONE | NONE | Not a FK target | — |
| `bill_items` → `menuitems` (via `server_menu_item_id`) | YES (LAZY, read-only) | NONE | NONE | NONE | `fk_bill_items_menuitem_tenant` (V3) | **RESTRICT** |
| `bill_items` → `itemvariants` (via `server_variant_id`) | NO (bare `@Column`) | — | — | — | `fk_bill_items_variant_tenant` (V3) | **RESTRICT** |

**Key finding**: The `bill_items.bill_id` cascade is **not represented in JPA at all**. The `@ManyToOne` on `server_bill_id` is a separate, secondary reference used only for JSON serialization on pull syncs. The real FK on `bill_id` has `ON DELETE CASCADE` in the DB but Hibernate has no `@OnDelete(action = OnDeleteAction.CASCADE)` to match. This means:
  - When Hibernate deletes a `Bill` entity (via `repository.delete(bill)`), it will try to `DELETE FROM bills WHERE id=?`. The DB cascade silently deletes child `bill_items` rows.
  - If Hibernate ever bulk-deletes bills and the persistence context has managed `BillItem` entities, Hibernate might try to issue individual `DELETE FROM bill_items` statements before the bill delete, or the `EntityNotFoundException` on stale references could occur.
  - **Since `Bill` has no `@OneToMany` collections**, Hibernate never issues child deletes. It only deletes the `Bill` row and relies on the DB cascade. This works but is fragile — any future addition of a collection with `cascade = ALL` on the `Bill` side would cause a double-delete attempt.

#### C. `bill_payments` → `bills`

| Relationship | JPA `@ManyToOne` | `cascade` | `orphanRemoval` | `@OnDelete` | DB FK | DB `ON DELETE` |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| `bill_payments` → `bills` (via `bill_id`) | NO (bare `@Column`) | — | — | — | `fk_bill_payments_bill_tenant` (V3) | **CASCADE** |
| `bill_payments` → `bills` (via `server_bill_id`) | YES (LAZY, read-only) | NONE | NONE | NONE | Not a FK target | — |

**Same pattern as bill_items**: `bill_id` has `ON DELETE CASCADE` at DB level, but no JPA mapping. The `@ManyToOne` on `server_bill_id` is read-only for sync serialization.

#### D. `marketplace_orders` → `bills`, `marketplace_orders` → `restaurantprofiles`

- **No JPA entity** for `marketplace_orders` (V21). Managed via raw SQL/repository queries.
- **FKs** (defined in V21):
  - `fk_marketplace_orders_restaurant`: `(restaurant_id) REFERENCES restaurantprofiles(id) ON DELETE CASCADE`
  - `fk_marketplace_orders_bill`: `(bill_id) REFERENCES bills(id) ON DELETE SET NULL`
- **No JPA cascade to worry about** since there is no entity. The DB handles it:
  - If a `restaurantprofile` is deleted → all its `marketplace_orders` are **cascade-deleted** (including order items via `fk_marketplace_order_items_order CASCADE`).
  - If a `bill` is deleted → `marketplace_orders.bill_id` is **SET NULL** (order record survives, just disassociated from the bill).
- This is correct behavior: marketplace orders are business records that should survive bill deletion.
- **However**: `marketplace_order_items` has `fk_marketplace_order_items_bill_item` with `ON DELETE SET NULL` on `bill_item_id`. So deleting bill items sets marketplace item links to NULL.

#### E. `device_registration_request` relationships

- **NO JPA relationships** at all. The entity has `@Column` fields only:
  - `restaurantId` (bare `Long`)
  - `requestedByUserId` (bare `Long`)
  - `matchedTerminalId` (bare `Long`)
  - `processedByUserId` (bare `Long`)
  - `assignedTerminalId` (bare `Long`)
- **No `@ManyToOne`**, **no `@JoinColumn`**, **no FKs** defined in V41 migration.
- **No cascade behavior.** These are just numeric references with no referential integrity constraints at the DB level.
- **Data integrity risk**: A `device_registration_request` can reference a non-existent `restaurant_id`, `user_id`, or `terminal_id`. The application code must enforce consistency manually.

#### F. Any cascade that could delete financial/audit records

**High-risk cascade chains:**

1. **Bill deletion** (DB-level cascade):
   - `DELETE FROM bills` → cascade-deletes `bill_items` and `bill_payments` (via `ON DELETE CASCADE` on `bill_id`).
   - `marketplace_orders.bill_id` is SET NULL (records survive).
   - **`payments` table is NOT cascade-deleted** (no FK constraint at all) — payments become orphaned.
   - **`security_audit_log` is NOT cascade-deleted** (no FK reference to bills).
   - **`stock_logs` is NOT affected** (no FK to bills).

2. **RestaurantProfile deletion** (DB-level cascade):
   - `DELETE FROM restaurantprofiles` → cascade-deletes `marketplace_orders` (via `fk_marketplace_orders_restaurant`).
   - Cascade from `marketplace_orders` → `marketplace_order_items` (via `fk_marketplace_order_items_order CASCADE`).
   - No cascade to `bills`, `users`, `categories`, `menuitems`, `itemvariants`, `bill_items`, `bill_payments`, `stock_logs`, `restaurant_terminal`, `device_registration_request`, `payments` — these all reference `restaurant_id` as a data column, not a FK. They become orphaned.
   - **Major gap**: Deleting a restaurant profile leaves all its financial data (bills, payments, etc.) orphaned with no FK integrity.

3. **MenuItem deletion** (DB-level RESTRICT):
   - `fk_menuitems_category_tenant` on `server_category_id` → RESTRICT (cannot delete if referenced)
   - `fk_itemvariants_menuitem_tenant` on `server_menu_item_id` → RESTRICT (cannot delete if variants reference it)
   - `fk_bill_items_menuitem_tenant` on `server_menu_item_id` → RESTRICT (cannot delete if bill items reference it)
   - `fk_stock_logs_menuitem_tenant` on `server_menu_item_id` → RESTRICT
   - **These RESTRICT constraints (added in V3) are a safety improvement** — they prevent accidental deletion of menu items that have transaction history.

4. **Category deletion** (DB-level RESTRICT):
   - `fk_menuitems_category_tenant` on `(restaurant_id, server_category_id)` → RESTRICT
   - Cannot delete a category that has menu items referencing it.

5. **`payments` table** (no FK, no JPA entity):
   - Has `bill_id BIGINT NOT NULL` but **NO FK constraint**.
   - Has `user_id BIGINT` but **NO FK constraint**.
   - Has `restaurant_id BIGINT NOT NULL` but **NO FK constraint**.
   - **Zero referential integrity.** This is the biggest audit/financial risk in the schema. Payments can point to deleted bills, deleted users, and deleted restaurants.

---

### Summary of Mismatches

| Entity relationship | JPA cascade/delete | DB `ON DELETE` | Match? | Risk |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `MenuItem` → `Category` | None | `RESTRICT` | No annotation, but JPA doesn't write this FK (read-only via `server_category_id`) | Low — FK prevents delete at DB level |
| `ItemVariant` → `MenuItem` | None | `RESTRICT` | Same | Low |
| `BillItem` → `Bill` (via `bill_id`) | **No relationship mapped** | `CASCADE` | **No** — Hibernate doesn't know about the cascade | Medium — works via DB trigger but fragile if collections added |
| `BillItem` → `MenuItem` | None | `RESTRICT` | Read-only | Low |
| `BillItem` → `ItemVariant` | None | `SET NULL` (V1) → `RESTRICT` (V3) | Read-only | Low |
| `BillPayment` → `Bill` (via `bill_id`) | **No relationship mapped** | `CASCADE` | **No** — same as BillItem | Medium |
| `StockLog` → `MenuItem` | None | `RESTRICT` | Read-only | Low |
| `StockLog` → `ItemVariant` | None | `RESTRICT` | Read-only | Low |
| `payments` → `bills` | **No JPA entity at all** | **No FK constraint** | **No** | **HIGH** — orphaned payment records |
| `payments` → `users` | **No JPA entity** | **No FK constraint** | **No** | **HIGH** |
| `marketplace_orders` → `restaurantprofiles` | **No JPA entity** | `CASCADE` | N/A (no entity) | Low — intentional cascade |
| `marketplace_orders` → `bills` | **No JPA entity** | `SET NULL` | N/A (no entity) | Low — intentional |
| `device_registration_request.*` | **No FKs at all** | **No FKs defined** | None exist | Medium — app-level integrity only |

### Critical Findings

1. **`payments` table has zero FK constraints** despite storing financial transaction data referencing `bill_id`, `user_id`, and `restaurant_id`. This is a data integrity and audit risk.

2. **`bill_items` and `bill_payments` DB-level `ON DELETE CASCADE` on `bill_id` is not represented in JPA.** While this works in practice (DB triggers handle it), it's an invisible contract. If someone adds `@OneToMany` collections to `Bill` with `cascade = ALL`, Hibernate would try to delete children first, then the DB cascade would attempt a redundant delete.

3. **`device_registration_request` has no foreign keys at all**, so orphaned references to users, restaurants, and terminals can accumulate.

4. **Deleting a `RestaurantProfile` orphans all its sync entities** (bills, users, menu items, etc.) because they reference `restaurant_id` only as a data column, not through a FK. The only cascade-delete is to `marketplace_orders`.

5. **The V3 migration hardened all `server_*` FK columns from `SET NULL` to `RESTRICT`**, which is a good safety measure for financial/operational data — you cannot delete a menu item that has bill items or stock logs pointing to it. This prevents accidental data loss.

6. **`security_audit_log` has no FK constraints** to any table (by design — it's append-only audit). It never gets cascade-deleted, which is correct.

7. **No `@OneToMany` collections exist anywhere in the entity model.** All relationships are unidirectional child→parent using the `server_*_id` + `@ManyToOne(LAZY)` read-only pattern. This means Hibernate's cascade/orphanRemoval mechanisms are entirely unused, and all referential action is driven by the Flyway-defined FK constraints.
```

```
| **KBOOK_ADMIN** | ~20 references (security config, JWT filter, sync exemption, IP allowlist, tests) | ~6 references (session check, normalization, DB migration) | ~5 references (route guards, sidebar, auth service routing) | **No impact** — current super-admin role. |

## Key Finding: V12 Migration Will NOT Break Anything

The V12 migration (`server/.../V12__collapse_legacy_user_roles.sql`) converts legacy `MANAGER`/`CASHIER`/`KITCHEN` user roles to `OWNER`. This migration has **already been applied** to production (it's in the migration history as V12). The current codebase:

1. **Server `UserRole` enum** contains only `OWNER`, `SHOP_ADMIN`, `KBOOK_ADMIN` — no legacy roles.
2. **Server authorization code** (SecurityConfig, @RequireRole, GenericSyncService, etc.) only references these three roles.
3. **Android `normalizeAllowedRole()` / `normalizeUserRole()`** already collapses any unrecognized role to `OWNER`.
4. **Android Room Migration 40→41** does the same DB-level collapse as server V12.
5. **Web-admin** only deals with `OWNER`, `SHOP_ADMIN`, `KBOOK_ADMIN` in route guards, UI conditionals, and API types.
6. **Legacy roles MANAGER/CASHIER/KITCHEN appear zero times** in any code that enforces authorization, defines user roles, or conditionally shows/hides UI.

The only occurrence of "KITCHEN" as a persistent concept is `PrinterRole.KITCHEN` on Android, which is a **printer profile role** (for routing tickets to the kitchen printer rather than the customer-facing receipt printer). This is entirely unrelated to user roles and unaffected by V12.
```

```
### Schema alignment
⚠️ **Minor discrepancy found.**

**Migration columns (V1 + later ALTERs):**
- V1: `id, local_id, device_id, restaurant_id, updated_at, is_deleted, server_updated_at, created_at, daily_order_id, daily_order_display, lifetime_order_id (NOT NULL), order_type, customer_name, customer_whatsapp, subtotal, gst_percentage, cgst_amount, sgst_amount, custom_tax_amount, total_amount, payment_mode, part_amount_1, part_amount_2, payment_status, order_status, created_by, paid_at, last_reset_date, version, cancel_reason`
- V13: adds `refund_amount NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0`
- V19: adds `public_token UUID NOT NULL`
- V25: adds `source_channel VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL DEFAULT ''`
- V26: adds `terminal_series, financial_year, invoice_series, invoice_sequence, invoice_number` + alters `lifetime_order_id DROP NOT NULL`
- V28: adds `created_terminal_id, created_device_id, current_owner_terminal_id`
- V40: adds `terminal_id`

**Entity vs migration comparison:**
- ✅ `lifetime_order_id` is `nullable=true` in entity, matches V26 `DROP NOT NULL`
- ✅ `refund_amount` is nullable in entity, but DB has `NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` — this is fine (Hibernate doesn't require `nullable=false` for NOT NULL columns; it uses defaults)
- ✅ `cancel_reason` has `columnDefinition="TEXT DEFAULT ''"` in entity — V1 has `cancel_reason VARCHAR(500) NOT NULL DEFAULT ''`. TEXT vs VARCHAR(500) — this is a type difference but likely doesn't cause runtime issues with Hibernate's `ddl-auto=validate`? Actually Hibernate might see `TEXT` vs `VARCHAR(500)` as different. This is a **potential mismatch**.
- ✅ `source_channel` matches V25 exactly
- ✅ `public_token` matches V19

**Issue:** `cancel_reason` in entity is `TEXT` but V1 defines it as `VARCHAR(500)`. If Hibernate `ddl-auto=validate` is on, this could fail validation.
```

4. The V12 role collapse is safe - MANAGER/CASHIER/KITCHEN have zero references in current authorization code.

6. device_registration_request needs restaurant_id → restaurantprofiles.id and requested_by_user_id → users.id FKs.
7. The Bill.cancel_reason TEXT vs VARCHAR(500) type mismatch could cause ddl-auto=validate issues.
8. source_channel backfill discussion needed.

## P0 — Verified Findings

### 1. `payments.bill_id` has NO foreign key constraint

**Confirmed.** V7 creates `payments` with `bill_id BIGINT NOT NULL` but no `REFERENCES bills(id)`. This is the most serious integrity gap — orphaned payment records, cross-restaurant payment references, and phantom bill references are all possible.

No JPA entity exists for `payments`, so Hibernate never validates this. All access is via native queries.

**Recommended fix:** Add tenant-scoped FK after validating existing data:

```sql
-- Check for orphans first
SELECT p.id, p.restaurant_id, p.bill_id
FROM payments p
LEFT JOIN bills b ON b.id = p.bill_id AND b.restaurant_id = p.restaurant_id
WHERE b.id IS NULL;

-- Add the constraint
ALTER TABLE payments
  ADD CONSTRAINT fk_payments_bill_tenant
  FOREIGN KEY (restaurant_id, bill_id)
  REFERENCES bills(restaurant_id, id)
  ON DELETE RESTRICT;
```

### 2. V12 role collapse is SAFE

The audit confirms **zero references** to `MANAGER`, `CASHIER`, or `KITCHEN` as user roles anywhere in current code:

- **Server `UserRole` enum:** Only `OWNER`, `SHOP_ADMIN`, `KBOOK_ADMIN`
- **SecurityConfig:** Only the three current roles
- **All `@RequireRole` annotations:** Only current roles
- **Android `normalizeAllowedRole()`:** Collapses unknown → `OWNER`
- **Web-admin route guards + UI:** Only current roles
- **`PrinterRole.KITCHEN`** on Android is a *printer type*, not a user role — completely unrelated

No privilege boundary was lost because no code ever granted different permissions to MANAGER/CASHIER/KITCHEN vs OWNER for any specific endpoint.

### 3. Missing Flyway versions (V27, V30-V39) are not a problem

No evidence these ever existed in production. The flyway_schema_history can be verified cross-environment but the gap itself is valid.

---

## P1 — Fix Before Production Expansion

### 1. `device_registration_request` needs FKs

No FKs at all despite referencing `restaurant_id`, `requested_by_user_id`, `processed_by_user_id`, `matched_terminal_id`, `assigned_terminal_id`. At minimum:

```sql
ALTER TABLE device_registration_request
  ADD CONSTRAINT fk_drr_restaurant FOREIGN KEY (restaurant_id) REFERENCES restaurantprofiles(id),
  ADD CONSTRAINT fk_drr_requested_user FOREIGN KEY (restaurant_id, requested_by_user_id)
    REFERENCES users(restaurant_id, id);
```

The terminal FKs (`matched_terminal_id`, `assigned_terminal_id`) should reference `restaurant_terminal(id)`.

### 2. `source_channel` backfill missing for POS bills

V25 backfills `source_channel` only for marketplace payment modes. In-store POS bills remain blank. This creates ambiguous reporting. Recommend:

```sql
UPDATE bills SET source_channel = 'POS'
WHERE (source_channel IS NULL OR source_channel = '')
  AND payment_mode NOT IN ('zomato', 'swiggy', 'own_website');
```

But check whether blank currently signals "legacy/unknown" before backfilling.

### 3. Cascade risk: RestaurantProfile deletion

No FK from any sync entity to `restaurantprofiles(id)` (they carry `restaurant_id` only as a data column). Deleting a restaurantprofile orphans every bill, user, menu item, payment, terminal, etc. Consider `ON DELETE RESTRICT` if restaurant deletion should be blocked when data exists, or add a lifecycle policy (soft-delete + scheduled purge).

### 4. `Bill.cancel_reason` type mismatch

Entity declares `columnDefinition="TEXT DEFAULT ''"` but V1 creates it as `VARCHAR(500) NOT NULL DEFAULT ''`. If `ddl-auto=validate` is enabled, Hibernate may reject this. Either align the entity to `VARCHAR(500)` or the migration to `TEXT`.

### 5. Missing indexes on common query paths

| Path | Index exists? |
|---|---|
| `payments(restaurant_id, bill_id)` | ❌ (V7 did not create one) |
| `bills(restaurant_id, invoice_number)` | ❌ (only composite on `(restaurant_id, financial_year, invoice_series, invoice_sequence)`) |
| `device_registration_request(restaurant_id, device_id)` | ✅ partial unique for PENDING, but no general lookup index |
| `marketplace_orders(platform_order_id)` | ✅ has its own index |

---

## P2 — Maintainability

### Tenant-scoped FK patterns (V3) are correct

All V3 FKs use `FOREIGN KEY (restaurant_id, child_id) REFERENCES parent(restaurant_id, id)` with the supporting `ux_*_tenant_id` unique indexes. This prevents cross-restaurant references.

### The `server_*_id` read-only pattern

Every `@ManyToOne` in the sync entities uses `insertable=false, updatable=false` on `server_*_id` columns. These are *read-only* JPA relationships used for JSON serialization on sync pulls. The *real* FK columns (`bill_id`, `category_id`, `menu_item_id`) are bare `@Column` longs with no JPA relationship. This is an intentional dual-key pattern for offline sync.

### No `@OneToMany` collections exist

Zero cascade/orphanRemoval directives in JPA. All child cleanup is handled by DB-level `ON DELETE CASCADE` (on `bill_items`, `bill_payments`). This works but is invisible to Hibernate — adding any `@OneToMany` in the future would risk double-delete.

---

---

# KhanaBook Database Schema Report

## Architecture Overview

**Stack:** Java 17 + Spring Boot + PostgreSQL (server) ↔ Kotlin + Room + SQLCipher (Android)
**Sync:** Offline-first with `(restaurant_id, device_id, local_id)` identity key on all core tables
**Tenant isolation:** `restaurant_id` on every record; V3 hardened FKs to composite `(restaurant_id, id)`

---

## Feature → Schema Mapping

### 1. Offline-First with UPI QR

| What happens | Schema involved |
|---|---|
| Bill created offline on Android | `bills` with `local_id`, `device_id`, `is_synced=false` |
| UPI ID stored on device | `restaurantprofiles.upi_handle`, `upi_mobile` → synced server-side |
| Bill pushed when online | `bills.is_synced` → `true`, pushed via `/sync/master/push` |
| Pull back from server | `bills` returned with `server_id`, `server_updated_at` for reconciliation |

**Key columns:** `local_id`, `device_id`, `restaurant_id`, `is_deleted`, `server_updated_at`, `version` (on every sync entity via `BaseSyncEntity`)

### 2. Invoice Sharing (SMS + WhatsApp)

| What happens | Schema involved |
|---|---|
| Share via SMS | `bills.customer_whatsapp` — customer phone |
| WhatsApp link | `public_token` (UUID) → unguessable invoice URL |
| Invoice data | `bills.invoice_number` (e.g., A07), `bills.total_amount`, all item data via `bill_items` |

### 3. KOT + Dual Printer

| What happens | Schema involved |
|---|---|
| Customer receipt printer | `restaurantprofiles.printer_name`, `printer_mac` |
| Kitchen printer | `restaurantprofiles.kitchen_printer_name`, `kitchen_printer_mac` (V2) |
| Printer role on Android | `PrinterRole.KITCHEN` / `PrinterRole.CUSTOMER` (Android only, not in server schema) |
| KOT items queued | `bill_items` with `is_synced=false` until KOT print + push |

### 4. Google ML Kit (Menu Extraction)

| What happens | Schema involved |
|---|---|
| Photo captured → OCR → structured data | `menu_extraction_jobs` — stores raw extraction + status |
| Extracted items → menu | Written to `categories` + `menuitems` + `itemvariants` |
| ML Kit runs on-device | No server round-trip needed; works offline |

### 5. Multi-Terminal Support

| What happens | Schema involved |
|---|---|
| Terminal registration | `restaurant_terminal` — server-owned registry (V26) |
| Device request flow | `device_registration_request` — PENDING → APPROVED flow (V41) |
| Per-device invoice series | `bills.terminal_series`, `financial_year`, `invoice_series`, `invoice_sequence`, `invoice_number` (V26) |
| Per-device daily order | `bills.daily_order_id` + `terminal_series` + `last_reset_date` |
| Terminal ownership | `bills.created_terminal_id`, `current_owner_terminal_id` (V28) |
| Terminal sync scoping | `bills.terminal_id` backfilled via `restaurant_terminal` join (V40) |

**Uniqueness:** `ux_bills_restaurant_invoice_series_active` — `(restaurant_id, financial_year, invoice_series, invoice_sequence)` WHERE `is_deleted=false AND invoice_number IS NOT NULL`

### 6. Pay-Before-Food vs Pay-After-Food

| What happens | Schema involved |
|---|---|
| Restaurant config | `restaurantprofiles.order_payment_flow_mode` = `'pay_before_food'` / `'pay_after_food'` (V24) |
| Pay-before: single sync | One bill push + pull cycle |
| Pay-after: draft → complete | Bill pushed twice: first as draft (`order_status='draft'`), then as completed |
| Payment tracking | `bill_payments` — per-leg payment splits with `payment_mode`, `amount`, `gateway_txn_id` |

### 7. Server-Owned Payments (Easebuzz Gateway)

| What happens | Schema involved |
|---|---|
| Gateway config stored server-side | `restaurant_payment_config` with encrypted salt (V7) |
| Payment created on server | `payments` table — `bill_id`, `amount`, `gateway_txn_id`, `payment_status` |
| Webhooks received | `easebuzz_webhook_events` — raw payloads (V6) |
| Webhook audit | `payment_webhook_logs` — signature validation + processing status (V7) |
| Refund tracking | `payments.refund_*` columns — mode, status, amount, reason, gateway IDs (V14, V17) |

---

## Verified Integrity Issues

### P0: `payments.bill_id` has no FK constraint

`payments` references `bills` but has `bill_id BIGINT NOT NULL` with no `REFERENCES`. Can produce orphan payments. Add `FOREIGN KEY (restaurant_id, bill_id) REFERENCES bills(restaurant_id, id) ON DELETE RESTRICT`.

### P1: `device_registration_request` has zero FKs

References `restaurant_id`, `requested_by_user_id`, `processed_by_user_id`, `matched_terminal_id`, `assigned_terminal_id` — none have FK constraints. Add FKs to `restaurantprofiles(id)`, `users(id)`, and `restaurant_terminal(id)`.

### P1: `Bill.cancel_reason` type mismatch

Entity uses `TEXT`, V1 migration creates `VARCHAR(500)`. May fail `ddl-auto=validate`.

### P1: `source_channel` blank for POS bills

V25 backfills only `zomato`/`swiggy`/`own_website`. In-store bills remain blank. Consider backfill to `'POS'` if blank doesn't carry legacy meaning.

---

## Clean Parts

- **Tenant isolation** (V3 composite FKs) is well implemented
- **V12 role collapse** is safe — no code references MANAGER/CASHIER/KITCHEN
- **All 15 JPA entities** align with Flyway migrations (except `cancel_reason` type)
- **Missing Flyway versions** (V27, V30-39) are valid gaps, not defects
- **`ON DELETE CASCADE` on `bill_items`/`bill_payments`** works via DB trigger; no JPA orphanRemoval risk (zero `@OneToMany` collections)
- **`ON DELETE RESTRICT` on `server_*_id` FKs** (V3 hardening) prevents accidental menu item/category deletion when transactional data references them

---

## 3. INTERACTION WITH THE `restaurant_terminal` TABLE

### Entity (`RestaurantTerminal.java`)
- **Table**: `restaurant_terminal`
- **Columns**: `id` (PK, auto-increment), `restaurant_id`, `terminal_series` (unique per restaurant), `terminal_name`, `device_id`, `is_active`, `status`, `credential_version`, `created_at`, `updated_at`
- **Unique constraint**: `ux_restaurant_terminal_series` on `(restaurant_id, terminal_series)`
- **Indexes**: `idx_restaurant_terminal_restaurant` on `restaurant_id`, `idx_restaurant_terminal_status` on `(restaurant_id, status)`

### Repository (`RestaurantTerminalRepository.java`)
Key queries:
- `findByRestaurantIdAndTerminalSeries(restaurantId, series)` — standard lookup
- `findAndLockByRestaurantIdAndTerminalSeries(restaurantId, series)` — **pessimistic write lock** for invoice sequence allocation (serializes concurrent invoice number generation per terminal series, PLAN section 5)
- `findByRestaurantIdAndDeviceId(restaurantId, deviceId)` — device-to-terminal binding lookup
- `findByRestaurantIdOrderByIdAsc(restaurantId)` — list all terminals
- `countByRestaurantIdAndStatus(restaurantId, status)` — count for 5-terminal limit enforcement
- `findByRestaurantIdAndStatus(restaurantId, status)` — filter by status

### All Write Paths (who writes to this table)

| Operation | Method | Location |

| Heartbeat (update timestamp) | `POST /sync/terminal/activate` (Case 1b) | `TerminalController.java` line 257 |
